AppNexus Eyes Mobile Leadership

 

In a video interview on Bloomberg, CEO Brian O'Kelley of real-time ad platform AppNexus talks about his recent mobile deal with mobile ad network Millennial Media to create an exchange (read that AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tebBPzVwJ3VSqQi9HYcRvJaQ9jnvq727OeqUpnVHpoVvYsNRuPvLBJk4lxDMixwFeBCmp1jSgT9D2cJ7-cCnjg-v3dVqWLBIbPi_G8qNfs6fNpd-Ee4pbWNf7lM46Z6waxJOMqXM9a6opI40zBi01fPr43GZJTat4COUYj6ydUxDy_f4c1OUR5BsfQPBeTct8eAUrTrZ10IonJcR8D7UbX7GWUgj8wV6QY=> ). He says his company will be the leader in mobile "probably next year sometime" and has no plans in the next year or two for an IPO until "predictability and scale" are in place. See the interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tcUodvnk7wAUmwvEC7UZEoaTGl1qFH0WQCDsuYlDzYGfR9G7a9v8Cgo4yJ2buP1RKukr86EK8ohk0GIvaxYGEqLUtrBz5MN3UD3qBvWufVVZ6TaDJiqYkhxmUmMFW_NNGBvkYD00VM9sTxBp5ZmIkUo2-ES4P1q4VI6yMQL3_60j_Rs1dmebZAvS5zCko-zmhyR-YO1meX8tNC0bPcqYTkUeRjQelLZDGI=> .

 

Facebook Algos And Ads

 

Facebook is changing its ads algorithm to try and deliver more relevant ads in users' news feeds. According to a post on Facebook's Newsroom site, marketers could see variation in ad distribution as user feedback is taken more into consideration. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tfScdo3fPUD0DRD-pPMtltgxFl5bVecWjjXt_llTvxTwIsSJnkjn6Cx4d9FR_zn3rata8MlXot9zw5WAEIbXkstn0q9xm7FkZWKgrQnVK0N-XROsQcsvb2IzvDIWBMgiDuzFb4BDwY2ymeXOlxSFFNMtBneZHklehJXlZ7Tu1hhAvaDFmT3un4D> . Meanwhile, Datalogix CEO Eric Roza tells Business Insider about his company's deal with Facebook and says, "'A 3X return on ad spend, or greater, is pretty typical [on Facebook]. It compares very favorably' to the traditional media buys, like TV, that grocery brands are comfortable with." Read that one <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tdIKl7UaH8QW4ttAltKspQsu4ohHVVyZ3htPOqcNN6U2z1c-ah22V455eGNkqI_ULnghCcdGblJuj3lRpx-B9OoOhW7EBkejjeWbRhEBoOAi2obWsjQ2Wdr6-SaVNLM60twBMKuhBmaT6ZRW80MFw8df0Epehzk7Ks=> .

 

The States Of Mobile

 

Web browser company Opera analyzed mobile traffic to create its latest State of Mobile Web report. According to its results, traffic and engagement are out of sync: Mornings are spent in "lean-forward" activities including shopping and research while afternoons are spent in "lean-back" activities like checking the news and browsing entertainment sites. The wee hours are spent on career and personal finance sites. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tcmbWLXovPN9rOQrKgij8Z5YuEynqwdCBxITSzZ2u2Ik-P7SmBkaPN0npvZLGBF5hGtY5af1XEEkS1FTTo0JymalmdJaS7vwnxYEik3pm0jstdpy-Bp3YuVK8i1rgHGVBfE4R_1_e-7q2V2S5DICgdpn1uvxH1PYlU=> .

 

The Creative In Ad Week

 

Advertising Week is officially over, and a lot of new trends were discussed in front of the 90,000 or so attendees across New York City. The New York Times covered a couple of the bigger panels, including one that focused on creative in the now very technological advertising industry. "The more technology expands, the more challenging it is to know what to make," said Saatchi & Saatchi New York exec Peter Moore Smith. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tcbiSS2Nwg_bV_FidZNvmqFmb-f7_N0yYAi7HXiQjHTKKLyF7sjeCl3P4xG0j4XWiqPgR7zP5kNwGUcIPAmnvek3zqaOVlq_CT2st9YjtKER-2qFBp3PbPrWXtBiPeOFZeWCIS-VidCJ3iTAOU-3Z_skOO49CpefOE572v5bZ9LyIsvY9Luom7UBPC4yrFp8kNfXCdGLq1fqFnyRHxgsGcUrrzxKIqYounWqHoUZJg6izIJYGcSBu7r> . And read kbs+ exec Darren Herman's take on the week here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tcDMR4NZ2HeBETcsDFE0yxOm3nRFKtq7YYwi5jj_9HFQRxMLy4ctCakselkxju0aIqnG48YBiBQMFUhoxaPNnX_4whF-qEXGq3JOEfECXPPxFy6op8y2_eZCLHbloodEzNV4nhqZRKOt4TArUuNPo_NQ4CrrP-xEu2a7yVSTPPsXyTkDNW-C8M8wxWz2Val7Yc=> . Finally, Ad Age's Alex Kantrowitz takes a look <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tesYK9A3HbelV2Y6K2QsF0avgK0RyHzOVxCUQx7pcd0EmeUX8wy1I1G6BFTERSAzB6QaTXybkT05TCyUdq34yxJy-I_a-fRrSaOAm5KcHWIOPFvg8QRrUSOx3NORCI12Isayq-Pgg1NWnwv3JhN8k25eXCJOMNMXqpHO147bbsI6Fb5DJNdJdYn2BdYQ265NFc2meStEYyvq_-GCXDbzFWKqUrr2qK6SsEvTbSGaIQrqQ==>  at "over-hyped" trends that fell short last week.

 

Twitter Closing The Loop

 

On Marketing Land, Matt McGee notes the addition of website analytics to Twitter's follower and timeline activity. McGee says, "You can see tweets that link to any specific page on your website. You can see how often Twitter users click on links to your website, or to any specific page." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tfXuJydQVwwtwNcOmVtxAnT9T8tN16_7WqjQPI1qqYSfIYxo4JnJIbc5qTU0d9nvkI7Lh-gPiqALVXaxz5IGG_hB63P0m1laI7yh3pmubU5JcJWLaMLVi677Ak8t3CKCmixnqlhVbBQYepSAjZoW60waTYIQMqF74mcs9v-dLNTiIC2eBMsLJ7LcfyR4vGjd1g=> . Twitter is helping close the loop for publishers on its importance to publishers' overall traffic. Twitter's exchange through MoPub should benefit eventually as publishers sign up.

I'll Have To Get Back To You

 

On The Makegood, Underscore Marketing's Tom Hespos offers four tips to the marketer on knowing when an agency may not be putting its best foot forward. At No. 1, Hespos offers, "Your agency can't answer simple questions on the spot. Everything you ask about, whether it's a closing date for a print insertion to a question about how you're tracking a KPI in your analytics package, is met with an 'I'll have to get back to you.'" Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001SCwg2VOw3tf07qmkHG0QgKvI4pS6YDy86mvPyFmXh_fF_yLK9lnup8JN4w9bFWqUjPcNQjS3_JPJYAqbrJi3R_WLwRgeon5VGC6oO3cPlk6ZtU-W1AGMOsJsj7JGuJe-lCn6y4oHhGxac7miY0gwFT_Qsn6giLSzV-4rgRqUukMQgXAsQ792O_ffuOjM_aLocpP4lhjfwFEX3Aqxr0-Dirm0uEOw1h3OLdU-v7cfunU=> .

Weather Moves To The Exchange

 

IPONWEB and The Weather Company say they are partnering on a weather-based advertising platform. The release states that this isn't just about targeting through Weather Channel owned-and-operated websites: "Weather can now leverage this targeting for extension campaigns purchased on a real-time buying basis across multiple exchanges and supply sources beyond Weather's own properties. Weather will also utilize IPONWEB's recently launched BidSwitch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInrm3T0AwEQVpO8dj8Lru5Fjyu82jmCvANtsZqP6Vbal0Y0MpXIf9LGD1jfNYBcc7rCA3SFwqHpY8Ot_WXBr-6paHw7GUFLIJKTXFrYJAahxvgggF2oMCzArx-XVzsido6cqZGTOEgxk9RK-Giv-qJP62amqcyit0lReczV7JkbjUUJ2-l3OaKWPAiTCFCDXlQUz2KAy4CS_Iw4VdWLiHVgM>  to access this inventory." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInp-eXUd4cXGdsT6X7kcVKKCHLdOTsEwx7q2N6DGhUd2PHh_w2JJOvlnqYyC5dVhd_ASY84Av4zzqkCPThSGbZ6TB1YsG_oaVvDK1wpsq4suEpK8bDt-ySYCszDG-yE0VcW71xDQ5Kz28m37kTFCcASZGmFUHAG4mcQn_G2IfClr-dYaFqVMoy8FscDlNq03fyaP2bUSH9EhV-LIP3t9xQ0Li14LdKAzth2c3Kbx1aLkMA==> .

 

Search (Retargeting) Update

 

Google has updated the "guts" of its search engine, as The New York Times' Nick Bilton reports. Users can use more complex queries to get answers -- rather than the old way of keyword matching. Bilton adds, "Yet Google revealed few details about how the new search algorithm works or what it changed. And it said it made the change a month ago, though consumers may not have noticed a significant difference to search results during that time." Changes were evidently implemented a month ago. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInosGH6_6k-9pj989lU-W0Y2vqZNp4jROUxz_KRcHf_DA5BTtS9_pwPicqtgksGD_n-HwZgTTnk81kv0N8XeagrFRVHohYseuS0hdrfZ0cs3ATDE1ppVemyZ5Rg3sO8QOdOP8-H7sACoWUT3PRxkHNf4lV6onFiX0xfkcseFgNX4H7oeaOABqVUa9kInjXYtc3-WcNAmU5A2w3T2s-1sUntD> . Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInosGH6_6k-9pj989lU-W0Y2vqZNp4jROUxz_KRcHf_DA5BTtS9_pwPicqtgksGD_n-HwZgTTnk81kv0N8XeagrFRVHohYseuS0hdrfZ0cs3ATDE1ppVemyZ5Rg3sO8QOdOP8-H7sACoWUT3PRxkHNf4lV6onFiX0xfkcseFgNX4H7oeaOABqVUa9kInjXYtc3-WcNAmU5A2w3T2s-1sUntD> . And, read the Google Inside Search blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInpTn12mPAGcqTatvx4DtPnEHJNzY7rBGFGhP1hfJE7gI8TQPs9P80WdDjchIebDvsQR0coMY8syDaHqTK-i2ymcX1Pbm_8nwBOGaoqU0Z4WZJewQLOW2Gyv_zaZeD5udi5ZlT8L8u62ZUmAV0f1GZFFBIGtNr_Jntx1ih0_29pXiNWM_fys_EKKmK0GgwG23Bs=> . It will be interesting to see how this plays out for Google search retargeting across digital channels when Google eventually, inevitably, unveils the tactic. It would seem targetable "audience" becomes more nuanced.

 

Amazon Disrupting CPG

 

A new report from Sanford C. Bernstein shows that ecommerce is shaking up the CPG industry by making pricing and demand more unpredictable for brands. As Ad Age points out, the brands who are popular on sites like Amazon are different from those that dominate physical stores. From the report: "Given that lower prices, specialized niche selections and delivery convenience seem to be the key drivers for consumers to purchase online, the outcomes for large incumbents may not be entirely positive." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInoLArvl7cVA8JRpZCuJQFTm8ZlJELp2Ytuysun9Gf8QCPpWHZCYKWWcoQPAtm7fUs8nbXRWeR2b2EQhdFol3EBCyzNQUN9T4KY5jr1VXrksGxU_l0rbfcztA-N2raMHmej9w0I9bTOhCae0cYFFEhzsMIvDaK5G90wjyrULVAV6Cjz5fETaf3QSPu3IdKMt-GA=> .

 

Going Direct

 

While image-sharing site Imgur has not taken a single dollar of investor money, it's profitable and its traffic numbers put it in the top 30 websites. The company also has no long-term business development plans and relies solely on an ad network and subscriptions for revenue, finds VentureBeat. The company's founder and CEO Alan Schaaf tells VentureBeat that eventually the company would like to handle its own advertising and work directly with brands to strategically place ads on the site. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInqTWajmCjwjH3xS5BC9Md_7cgqgmYZTcJ1yqmJcJnkpedpTagZbrgN8wkyV2m9bYhyW1hS6e1XYsbmZa-ETezR_2e6Vtpa9q6Dsvbew-jzFee2Z7Zzoi3LPW4r3dQY6UO_dbyhBTXFadisbgrcYLqGmPKELb7JpLJ5lSLsG4zRLFA5lo0mL46bM> .

 

Organic Search vs. Paid Search

 

A study from Kenshoo and Resolution Media <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInr_q4vwfIhhylUDHLSWf3ntAQ5g7ALdIdN2hV3lMncGWYEv2muMRLW8tqCBavfEQivv5780nlL92P5XQJP5pNMEMRE63ayidpligIOR1wjEZh308SfTFAWh3ynoIRF1D7M=>  analyzes paid and organic search marketing to uncover the effectiveness of each. Findings include: Consumers still click on paid ads even when organic ads are in the first spot and organic search drives higher brand-term metrics. Download the report <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInqCGI185UU3FqBlqehxJIlQKMyEyDivv5cv3x2n1P-mZFHcN1iFjOkvQU3W1d-kMok-6dcn89fPYk-DFFrgPR4aycP6_-_lroyqFL6hgFQIkbGS1oDxoTzexyZ-x9SlLPe37SE_Dh_edYU1BJ98RfIh8gISxhYvVUU=> .

News Publisher Ad Growth

 

FT.com reports that publisher MailOnline's ad revenues have grown 45% this year as its newspaper parent struggles on the print side. FT.com's Robert Brudden offers a few reasons, including: "Earlier this year MailOnline began rolling out an affiliate marketing initiative that links editorial content on its site to online vendors in a pioneering trial that could be mirrored by other online publishers. Last month, unique monthly browsers to MailOnline hit a record 138m, a 30 per cent increase on the same period last year." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInqlFCi0sAY15li75BneByoy3hlJy2kfznA2_PS--P9jkeop-u8jQthj-f0S76RSq2wVx_3vUkDb-PGLKJduW1zHjlRwGsKYYuduN88gMA3j3amlgxzUqsAxzWSvfqbivXmq0jT6NMC2Cqo_xaiCF_ibJl5kqZo675QprGhULqbGwgyjsR0LZhZy> .

 

Paywall Future

 

USA Today doesn't have plans for a paywall, although president and publisher Larry Kramer told Poynter they're studying it. The company is also raising the price of its daily paper from $1 to $2, which will also lead to the removal of some of its white boxes. Also, The Nation is planning to implement a paywall, according to Folio. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yt4BLOswInpv15S8H-sNXYNxX9vpB8emKP6QcPrDwEiKM5T3aX7kb8Fjkyo-pnwPiKrfJhJuT4uvbHkI9a9f_X3_7PlRr9uFc2tJsiBIyUVGJSYgSoJC8n4NtoYxP0gP2XPl5iirLP6c4SmcccSFZMS5Nkh6oK9yMy8hPrYHev3izi_g6lmWxhsaNBWWcIomucZctHLrGVzN3UA--_gJTIQHDHlekrhuR0vnzgVoHJg=> .

Invite Media 2.0 Goes Global

 

In an update to its DoubleClick Advertiser blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajaQl2KwwO63MD_VgE6EnA0soQSoom8P0yfJqFtqSX_Wpdpr_GzyJcUdbyaU4Ma8A8vRu8RJWZRZabOaJgVDKiK9RHYL6cW20oh2DmYZIBLAYVkVYbg2oTZZoksE9nT21x7kRiNji8FFfdDfSNESy-XzHqp-X_sowNGvgQ4XGTcPNGRl1HbnoVURf3hajYqqt7tKSY8-B6dvag==> , Google announced that Invite Media 2.0 (the demand-side platform it acquired in 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajZMiejjrIOdxG4YwY6qAmKQkR5TzsY9wb3G3jIplvYlLSxQiHfx91XWD39otmQPC2r249bZ6pkcYWe44n-o8mfy9PTxIgSgq1LC-me4HeTwFXxUZgL_DqgJWRIq4l_nefxF6GM7OtUJ0uQpqg9qU5U_j-rPNxAMjBOoYTSdx41b0w==> ) has finally rolled out globally. The updated platform is called DoubleClick Campaign Manager and it integrates the DoubleClick For Advertiser UI with DoubleClick Bid Manager. Some of the changes include workflow, ad formats, audience features and reporting. Google is also bringing dynamic creative (Teracent? <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajYY5Vv5osBiU0_mhUkt7mQ9luByvMnxp__A8bW8SsntSGl7qemkrV_3QdqwAjeBOj2gjbN8U0Vd8Hh1NJbGYzQXpcGvzjCO6Jokp9ehSTXPqEiSgJkW06UYmGSnGYNFf9FRxLHIdkgFmS7_cIhTOK6R7m64x08r0Y-YiwxfTVX3Ag==> ) capabilities to its AdWords platform to help small and medium businesses, according to a post on its Inside AdWords blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajbWPMx8p-HsDfEo07w7DVrLdqUzqPSylHySpjZWSOx_gONbYDud03kumeKu70dY6NSm1Q6V-BJFkWgpBgOYuIyzERDPtAehVRbHkI7njE0Wu1x3X3xrGfMsP96UowRDu6qqJF7ha5s2oIO6IODeyx-QNLcaWA3XcubX9Q_FOipPPNh8aS6Z9p2T8q17Mjdwabg=> . One product, Ready Image Ads, will automatically construct display ads that can then be customized based on a provided URL.

 

Amazon's Big Ad Plays

 

Amazon is firmly planting itself in the advertising space, Wired points out, as it seeks to move from ecommerce to a tech giant. According to eMarketer, Amazon is poised to bring in around $250 million more in ad revenue than Twitter. With its vast amounts of first-party shopping data, Amazon creates interactive ad units that allow consumers to buy a product from anywhere on the Web. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajZ9EH02iIMlJywk38NgMr8uTRkj4FhFomrdsAstwVt_3y-dIRWddZZu6aeiRPgsp_Z6uhXnvZUpgFHZru1CMVp6oCwVBwPU09GSYQ3ctQzY0C1rGh4VcSkv4niAD0ecq4TpG_R1CBMqslM5PCPeC3tf_yvOoPSuVvoR1kTsFYcfUw==> .

 

User-Gen Banners

 

Brands are very interested in user-generated content, but getting rights to use that content has been a tricky business. Chutes, a media rights services, hopes to make it easier for companies to gain rights to content by acting as an intermediary (remember the digital "syndication" craze in the early 2000s?). The Next Web spoke to CEO and co-founder Ranvir Gujral about how Chutes facilitates this process, which is by giving a user some sort of code that serves as permission. Chutes can also turn that content into banners ads for brands. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajbdxQVXl7vS5IZHh0rVZiRlCvpeYWuqBjIeJKXglZMm4HwCDItvTrINWdj5PQZplQHxfBAUmWA_cNTIJw9-lGvLAG9R9t7PPf04Z0T3nm98K-iiVMllnM7DKn2F9jzXlD6oCQItXr9f5y9iR3_7AiVvUOtquKzr7XxZVM17GM4zsR6gIRZfBOzzeie5z0Vfhri0NwfJrk1yofspIVTKL7X9Rs_OydWjYwAKYk4q_0aw7xIBwL5uV0V-fkhcUMVDbCkVZEZ5boge9J8Oy1m5MjII> .

 

Breaking Ad

 

Breaking Bad has a lesson for everyone <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajZKyt-iG42DgwiOw9txZaymmlxRjV_R1Bs7GNDyJO35UfmUFYyuJPFawO3bBEL_S5YRQNCUb_PZcpdf_PEJH-ez-ZTp2NZYfbv89wLXBilKIuQfpKomIWJV2dF2Z57CTdNkNad20pO7PE7tpxtNDyuR5XQzB9pM9OlcOk-ULneCGQ==> , even advertisers. Doug Weaver points out on The Drift that some of the main pillars of advertising will at some point crumble. His optimistic side says that the industry will use its abilities to solve problems like viewability, but his cynical side points to the third-party cookie attitude of "we'll just do something else" as evidence that the industry is fractured. He writes, "I love the innovation, the courage, the invention, the people...all of it. I just want to see it all devoted to building great businesses -- and a great business -- that will stand the test of time." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajYYJnoGRUNEZTDbuUX6H_bX3bJt6cNjkHU0y_aGqMgw9Z_itLfZntdL6Pv9ogeF3Dt3AVLQeZUdWQpFJ7HU_O-8PcXRqTRreQKjvGSkASf5u8o7uhcZVzv73sRWMMPvtoI=> .

 

Super Local

 

Mobile ad platform 4Info is combining location data with purchase data to power its new AdHaven Bullseye HyperLocal platform. Catalina is incorporating this new technology into its own advertising solution as well. "The ability to employ a separate creative message specific to a defined location will ultimately drive lift and loyalty for the world's leading CPG brands while creating a powerful mobile experience for their customers," said Catalina's Chris Henger. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajZB7kUXPpm_PBzg3hL3Ew8feB2DjtzY7yvdZr2ZynOaCFa5HAoj_p2uoW93RKz8bjCKl1YUDnP73rXmI-w5eu3OxQtehmUulhwusv4kvwIcEQTnzooHH2aOOVekFHvG3BUcwZnyrLIgcTG47NVFfh1P_F0j4eqQQl64D1rFdFXqqvvplL4zjfJcMssxr7v0tqbsslnxab6fvuPyV2qJ9R9QMVl0uMYu4FnWMDfQJB-rxeJVMH0jqV1NNXdNTddTbjiL_LKgfIWrEA==> .

Data Investigation Heats Up

 

After Senator Jay Rockefeller's investigation into data brokers stalled, he turned to data collectors to find out what information they ask for from visitors and how it's shared. According to Adweek, the FTC is also looking into data brokers, as privacy concerns escalate. "While some consumers may not object to having their information categorized and used for marketing, before they share personal information it is important they know it may be used for purposes beyond those for which they originally provided it," Rockefeller wrote. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qlGgjBivajZoylOL3J-WWNzyFu12qOYbUy8HPn5d7fk7UimaTJqk0rB2rORaA7IdAoPgK4cyr3GSXAcm4ZPLvF4AtjVIZXeYIQ2NbIB_HlLauk5MpMAd1TAHdw3DTf8sJIaH8EFsC9AfGh6SRojDC7cUAwZweYkD-MYsSp5gf3EFiYh5dzEsbhz0fhlmzTsMYxdrKLKBY_kkD8F2WF3RHL_Nke2fm2rqn3HJ5yh86pnn_i6DhcZGSQ==> .

Facebook Transaction Data

 

Is Facebook now a payment processor? Not yet, but the social platform has taken one step closer to closing the loop on mobile commerce transactions. Last month, AdExchanger covered Facebook's foray into an "autofill" feature for beta brand JackThreads. Put simply, shoppers can use their Facebook login to populate payment info - removing one step from a sometimes less-than-stellar checkout process on mobile. Now, according to TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEhrIhdwOyUeqaUgbEPwBdV4Q_qWUi8I9rNri7mZI-3YAekCSWGEeDbExK-k_nDuc-4THKY7cf7YqEkqja3eE5uDQILOVw7ZtiWT0jYjIltEWhjYCaBOCn3D_VQ5oKE6CqlUFGucVUXpVK11NuKDPtzPsdx96XHZcmheaFODxlpieiJ0fxOkBz0FwVoJvG0AlVPSb4q4oSv7EC04u9VClVEQtRVVSPMefdlnIzsUlkepC_lwL6xcy5bg3zuolu8QAi0=> , Facebook has teamed up with PayPal, Stripe and Braintree to ramp things up on the processor side and product manager Deb Liu tells Josh Constine that Facebook is trying to help developers "monetize and convert." Facebook - getting closer to transaction data. Anybody want a Facebook credit card?

 

Reaching For Publishers

 

Pinterest announced a new pin, specifically for news articles, which gives more detailed information about a story including a photo, headline, publication name and story blurb. This isn't the first time Pinterest has tailor-made a pin -- recipes, movies and products all have their own formats. With all the talk of promoted pins, this could be a play to get publishers on board. Read the blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEgLPn-3MwXh9D8YG1zhzyt_61kxQJndwT0yKHBWwpxiXhNdE2RBB0InJlWXt6pT5h4q2k1XxijOntQQlEUebEojFWP63DqqtIJ4YuT8kv8qHcQPXJAJdaVbw1ho22ylpgDsXUPsSd2zoqT4f6OqY0cJkd--Dtz6EbgnMMfUjU7fDY_E7P1AOiRh2dW341A58U2-K1oKYERplQ==> .

 

Twitter Funds

 

According to The Street, Twitter will list on the New York Stock Exchange when it goes public, while looking to avoid the issues Facebook had when it went public. Twitter filed its S-1 confidentially, so most information about its IPO remains speculation. The Street's sources say Twitter will raise about $1.5 billion and have a $15 billion valuation. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEhWKbSREGZfaUnZJ-rLH87nW1AKfGk8yt-i-c61hhXugYPJ0XCi9luWt6vU2zIfYaWDK4BGJwNJunhiLHi1ixANVTQ_gVl3EeImaj3jWBvK72AJlpa8xGffjueCbceFhQ4iYzyf8lRM1hVPufiheBaseWddw6cpQL9vzjZuYCq5itZOw5W-Bl47Jp_Hg-bPrUVNU9ku2kKuAQ==> . Facebook raised $16 billion in its May 2012 IPO and was, initially <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEirhw6FqUH2DkyZLkntigZlKfYoiPpkKqElZNv1-Ado-9kWeq1RsHgCN4qNlKMcEWY6YL2eRwy9ia0KAjsc_x353MCJHXTvg1kKZXtPygPFh_cn6E5uqYL3HCkHoGRGQxidTE8L_Ner9qF_Pve5HZbmiwdB26lYqB6egEFwIUfoX60W07o9SAkmPhbicn-h-EU=> , valued at $104 billion.

 

Mobile Ad Lift

 

According to analytics/measurement firm comScore, mobile ads do work. The company has conducted hundreds of Mobile Brand Lift studies and compiled the results, with the biggest boost being purchase intent, at 28% lift. The company doesn't have a clear answer for why this is happening, but it could be related to the on-the-go nature of mobile, or social influences. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEjdLxFCk08Bw6UZTz6v45EXvuLZ6bEoTjjX92D-nEl5zVMloGzEOR-P6rKv519G5MDYOaWJvk8nJliDRCVFa-S3QMZQgQzIcI5-fd_eLQvwpi9z8CoUbBz4p-wQC-54y64bQFID1Tvq5CXEt9aXKZRdaNX8T_ZRvCv6vFPR8HwZ3UFBu31zjbA4J3G7q4POD6aEYkjoXF475g==> . Complementary read: An IAB survey of 300 brand advertisers found mobile ad spend has increased 142% from 2011 to 2013. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEg1cYUTgvbQGHpcUpsQ70ZGSJOeQDKz2rBsvbkb8o4RV3a_UktFDHL7DnJJpo4xHuZWQYdJom6MqL7aEzRWh09sw7ZOhwe-EAZ-tGlaEr0ZSTviSPCUO6KIDYdtrgqDsFzSWgtEzltflqOjPNHc-acXUBrQVXEJ24i779Km3nucbVw0EzZtIivNgiSjgtUDdHzRoCRzGfvzvglLIN2MqMqLO8A58AGv9QY=> 

 

Making Big Audience

 

In a feature piece on Ad Age, Michael Sebastian highlights Troy Young's first steps toward Hearst publishing's reinvention as president of its digital unit. Sebastien begins, "The industry is hoping that a more muscular Web presence could help it draw a larger audience and attract a greater share of digital spending, so Mr. Young's success or failure at Hearst will be closely monitored." Brand Marketer Invests

 

Brand licenser Iconix Brand Group (owner of Candie's, Roca Wear and other brands) has led an entire round of financing -- $20 million -- in media company/ad network Complex Media. Iconix CEO Neil Cole tells Business Insider that "the investment will yield strategic benefits for both Complex Media and Iconix, but not monetary. 'We think there are so many assets we can leverage, but unfortunately we don't own 100% of Complex,' Cole said." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cNUwD0OFYEg27JzfMhFTvEqdDft-kI41sPH-jU52PwGWutNGd167h17rQxdyyYAyQ_QBPqV80cIShKiyQZ0RvNMPwEDZDSYcCQQOQsC1FtMKL_AXjyVjKDutrt1EIXZMTOIo77QuPPcMosajHaGzHJ0Y63Ui015CD7baIAxnDxdo-mruui0EZCvuN7HsUaCv-gVIgpMg2-7z5SQ3YBmb4Q==> . Is this the future for a company like Glam Media or Alloy Digital: selling to a marketer seeking a digital marketing -- and programmatic -- strategy? Like "soap operas" digitally served.

Millennial Measurement

 

Millennial Media and Placed are teaming up to bring measurement tools to mobile. The new product will be called Omni Measurement Solutions and will allow advertisers to measure foot traffic, purchases and impact on high-funnel activities. "The product we're working on with Millennial Media allows advertisers to track conversions beyond the mobile device itself, and extend measurement into the physical world," said CEO David Shim of Placed. Look out for an upcoming partnership with comScore as well. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHNYc_SgZm9hX569MCCWxlCIgvpWQpm8PpwdVy1XlV8_KCNaucL9ULQ3xTshgHJzShDwJl1c8cGsZ-U0i1h-5JHFNFMu-bgVmUQxFnz76r0c4sUxzyXjYy2_mvjBtH-2P-SGpsePP5ELGjEv6cnomkug6xri0Uij-MZAyRHGCOAXdGh3x_UtCikULYNV4rAFlovIJqD8RKl9gX_cRtRFhEby-j6x8BcfHRpoOarEzONjwjSiGDDPzf2-Punv1Ehqn-SoW7pcvRJ0xA==> .

 

New IAB Video Ads

 

Yesterday, the Interactive Advertising Bureau (IAB) released its IAB Digital Video Rising Stars ad unit style guide and technical specifications for public comment. Included is a new unit called the "Ad Control Bar," which claims to permit "viewers to engage in multiple ways through an elegant interface that sits just above the player controls." See it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHNp43v0M1ErhiOHxkr0LrNux9sVs2ZpARqwxCrxYH9tWhJCAPrQcYy5vwGic3vZgsCHRG_rNy_rKTeHRPgqR9T9YqIGxda-RaWmhMBtQnQ0LI7omZYsJ4HIi9vTi04lpO9qm9zfiQd52g==> . And read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHPRirz6T3UjtWRslX_LM6B83ZPWpE1GMX4SYG3IfLbALFkkUKG-_xMLgwPePfl1boffAkioPQzVaJTjE0Z65LnwMoAe-Nr6BgPaSQhdtI9gUU_z3pyWPtJ3BLkLdDYC4jCCZ116b8OY9wn5glIyGKwJQdhpekkB83ftp8LqOTt7nqen2RfDZkUbQpmtLKE7S7Zo_jT6jt5Nb1NIkLZrHlRXVBzPL-WwTXY=> 

 

Programmatic TV

 

The Drum reports on an interview with Publicis VivaKi Global CEO Frank Voris: "'Digital TV and the like, as that rolls out and penetration gets deeper, you will see the lower [value] inventory going first, like it did with display, longtail. The premium space is still going to be held by the owners and sold in an experiential way,' he forecast on the future growth of programmatic buying." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHMGFh5u83F4ZibDuu1vIKYjRD1DKqLhrEmg8M0BFQ3UJcP4GfivcnT4drJzll2s4YEgCwSalFv_mMTz3bIcIu7FAuQZWhuCLfxohjpSjr3KO5pmHDv9tNEwT_fGwsRr6Ia4SGGkRzB6zu-NDYE0ianfPUyohh7KQhlrZh4X7PslTpQ8Fwqe-kEMrodpzqufFM2RUam-65I18y7iQQ54436eJOofy0cuyyZsLgqyzlilzzc4IH_5mxVQ> .

 

Smaller Is Better

 

The Omnicom-Pubicis agency holding company merger went under the microscope of The New York Times' Stuart Elliott in a short feature piece yesterday. He quotes Patrick Scullin, an executive creative director with 55-person creative agency Ames Scullin O'Haire, who says, "With Publicis and Omnicom coming together, independent agencies like ourselves are going to be the Davids going up against these Goliaths. I've yet to see a 'process' result in a better idea." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHPJVRws7fWod3h3ye5uMOh2iTaszMv6kFYISx--9vd_4imUUJ_su74XPpohBZ0QPATUSELJ7dOhGD9ZDP8qvxKE7J7zjVw0jPp3p8wWFlBEE9HDupGBQWqDlgqZXeiKtnWXTftRy-vBBoF6WtuEj2r3lTloDX1-Ac_kfhgqdAsha4ORd2bvOeVxLbAx206s7PmmWKLqgE-SHYjgewiV47GDRg1JRcDW2HH2CPI7huo5zw==> 

 

Contracting Agencies

 

Jack Marshall follows a similar thread to the NYT piece and looks at the programmatic effect on ad agencies in Digiday. He quotes R/GA's media maven, Tony Effik, who says "larger agencies need to contract if they wish to stay competitive. The way things are, they employ too many people and too many of the wrong people. Scale, he said, just doesn't mean what it used to mean." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHPToqJzCD6dgXoG4Jl73nm5w3OPiBP0IufE5zuqrk07tNgZO9artGE8NhfqQM7U0VQ4p2ubQdNg_DOP2LyCEAEY1iKh4e6mAKzgOdZL13UYMbPthSFKVLbbi0ha2ZXf8ZBODYKXgyxRuov482AbK68nVDRrWd4qa0WTQ18G6v_XHQ==> .

Define 'Programmatic'

 

In an Adweek interview, new AOL Networks CEO Bob Lord takes a crack at defining "programmatic media": "It's automating the mundane activities of matching audiences with inventory. So you have an audience that a marketer wants to get to. You have places that they visit, whether it's on the Web, mobile or video. And you want to match those audiences up with those advertisers and placements." Read the interview. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHNRYhk8jiSSXyPdJaeeWI6X_EK0UtgebYTYfnW_tMtNoiazpHky7RTPlmb5qJuaap4QsV03aLj-yQopHN1wAqkRDsnwrA5SGgEf3U4NRWjVb3e2CLWzAGXIRz8I53YNfjwi2XXtvQnjNK-yHT8JZRl1ZZ4Yck6AiqzbVXlRNcxgFD-CGtlcWNXwec-79BFogJbZZXl6aTkBo3sblglf3guf8f0SeMyklNStvEHhpSoIQg==> 

 

Job Stream

 

LinkedIn is building out its stream ads by introducing promoted jobs to the feed, according to AllThingsD's Mike Isaac. Given the success Facebook and Twitter have had with native advertising, it makes sense for LinkedIn to take one of its biggest ad types and put it where people will see it. The new ads will also work for mobile -- a huge part of social media advertising growth. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P_O3cNqQXHPzzjPovSYyc3r6jE8dUIZGj0rp44v41UOOH80oPt6TLcr2orYoThgoXQn0nYv5z7CLWnKL-xfANI_iOrnfe6QYf8ygTgd3BchNLd-Z9FtvGZslKRFQo3JlRTkB4PN9NRaEDsaTrp54CnWaAuR7OdrPre4H_qUjqU1wC8i99nX8Ee5bXgJuuOtC> .

Twitter Second-Screen Ads

 

As part of Advertising Week in NYC this week, Twitter will be talking up <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMXNyFD5zajjGub_Z5Tz3sC9fiPA8eZZqthJbqJ-EF9tyXU1RNXOeJWL4Tm5DI2rUOn3ae7xP8MewWS7Z_QmDyuzvm10P7QzFKYLX1jCWmWPz8VIUFForOr6KU2ncZRnF6i-RcKk568ZHGdtJtZwYxbYwvj7tPMEaIOPv58i-TCDDA==>  its TV products. The Wall Street Journal reports on the microblogging company's second-screen product, Amplify: "With Amplify, networks post short video replays on Twitter in near-real time. The video is sponsored by a brand. The network and Twitter each get a cut of the ad proceeds. (Twitter declined to detail the split.)" Read more on Twitter ad plans (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMWsUC8P2XkKs6HM23ewhVlwhRIjqhqY8z_zjMNTbAf0MZKzVJ8FEz_hu0DJ8RGsY59gbP1YXU2WFu5YdZS9yE8BtWl15IEjVkuiWF4RehsJsldTi039cNZrrfOYNZgANsZhrKwP56NkJTifyQX15cwoAU_ArXKSscsy5zvubnIBb_3pvc_XL5TD> . There's no mention of the MoPub acquisition, though, which could also augment reach of TV ad campaigns through Twitter.

 

The New Google Way

 

Google's forced transition of enhanced campaigns caused some advertisers to pull back, especially in retail, while others experienced better click rates and lower CPCs, according to Laurie Sullivan at MediaPost. The one sore spot for advertisers is results analysis. According to J.P. Morgan analyst Doug Anmuth, a focus on location and time of day will be more important going forward. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMV4PuXfn-IFr3GyZIDMMUxzGsy7sT6kspE_LT3qXVqYf18b_Adw6zlbAWUcZwRqV58PbXtuIdCHXi-bYQvVIeSovLPjRq5o4fTcclqggL06QBrPRGkmZM9b3_U4OnOX4712TAhNbdfEHsezMmd-VVCdIc3niGByZeXnVGIPuHy-FRI40R42Ib-e4kE4JtI4kDELTpSUEt_zzj3lNa__jyIOUSek3w7aynDi-qnIwYKUquPkaM70HggyG_QsqHwge1U=> .

 

Video Fingerprinting

 

TV ads will approach one-to-one addressability if advertising company Gracenote lives up to its self-inflicted promise. The Next Web's Paul Sawers reports on the company's video advertising personalization tech for connected TV devices: "The so-called video fingerprinting all takes place inside the TV - so we're not talking second screen, or third-party apps here. It goes on in the background without the user really knowing about it. It can of course fit into the bigger second screen picture." Of course. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMUODodmO4D9jtBxkyJJzrCQk2KWOOeDW9_O6x8h7dABEpkTI6Ev037EVALoeJjKTWS1aLgL6Fj3rxnjV8ms2kLzTvLQ9ygE1Sc62TFcXZ_Eb_hcQiWNm0bItBFp23wUI26jQu3vPZtBeu7FbASlwRIYhyPM4iekvgrp93HPXIzxRM8prtCUlNTW> .

 

Sports King

 

Fox Sports and YouTube are teaming up to bring Burger King ads to viewers in a deal arranged during the Digital Content NewFronts. Yes, there were deals at the NewFronts! Ad Age's Tim Peterson reports that the Fox Sports' YouTube channel has around 69,000 subscribers, significantly less than ESPN's, but the TV channel still has considerable reach. Fox Sports Digital's Marla Newman says the company is "definitely exploring" the possibility of bundling TV spots with the YouTube deals. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMWMNV4OegpqWt_tD7k96wcc4EtRyBrv6QHSn6Dkbvps-r0J-1ymdkN-trZ4eFEH7a8GxMK49ujWNGm0uXRcLyK8pPFFeSEn_De8bVvwa413yV6EsqIudGkdWlULxBsUKSLNf1nap6uV8IvL0K8ZUl9XpKBv25FPi5pOarlbUmW1z-Abw0qmAche> . Wonder what that Fox Sports' sales team structure looks like today? And tomorrow?

 

Rethinking Publishing

 

The New York Times' Nick Bilton reveals Gawker Media's latest publishing plans, known as the "Kinja <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMUDjaSGWluq8fvf_QGbMCO7srbYjU_EeSMj4wCtOaIRdeJCU3znUQ0qYJO6ErbHF2_CjnVEOj0PdMDqecjf0Itbu02cxI99aD8-c6VbG2Mh_jsj_UiVAn4F4_asiuxnnchu_sswY-ysww==> " platform. Publisher Nick Denton looks to further enable the reader as reporter, as Bilton explains: "When people sign up for Kinja, they are given their own Web address on the Gawker platform -- similar to a Tumblr Web site -- which becomes a collection of that person's comments on stories. Kinja will also enable readers to write headlines and summaries - comments that have graduated from college, if you will -- for stories on Gawker and even from other sites." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMUFvjSz7W-kKhFgEOf8-syzjp43iTPIWwaEpPpHMGTFEjI_ceNkH-KiKFq2-CU7kMGOIplrpsjhLLaIlQzGqknvYtKYU8qBEkBDxQPWrpitt-OnqOQlaXHu2ZWTCG_-Hjg6CBuzyA1CIOpk0ltpoOVOi1jkK3myarNUvnVmWLTmQqRK-axssZ8FJdzGiboccDQtDniQuZ-M0YZVCuZED-Wh5LoLLdWZr8-IVQNhGQE4SQ425BeSsivN> .

Cross-Platform Bedfellows

 

The Federal Trade Commission has let Nielsen know that even though it has acquired people-counter Arbitron for $1.3 billion, it must continue to make widely available Arbitron "Portable People Meter" service for eight years. In addition, as Variety's Todd Spangler details, "Under the terms of the FTC's approval, Nielsen must continue to support Project Blueprint, the cross-platform project measuring TV, radio, PC, mobile and tablet engagement that ESPN has been working on with Arbitron and comScore." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMVZOSVrFaOf874V8qyC2a6rDOyo6y1LAnc6PNxQPlGOdnA3c3hGWZmRd0CdD6pa0SyC4DfklqOAQFChBskC3_kjUAfveEheKmzvfkjYNj8o-YdBX7AL1BHXFNILLjv1dJynkT2JRLJY1ns7gWU26dQ97o3afjVyKmZNNmDkneFQntgn5VpXSQM4jh-5hjepp_KINgSEUvsctvifrW6B__zlW1ODpkUO4udX1F_B3ArzcEXjcmMYo-X1D_xELAUbdYw=> .

 

Why Rocket

 

After his company's surprisingly successful debut in the public markets, Rocket Fuel CEO George John tells the WSJ's Money Beat blog that "Rocket Fuel's big data use 'really helped' with general tech investors on the road show. 'A lot of people were talking about big data, and a lot of them wanted to know more about the [artificial intelligence] business on top of it,' he said." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=00187WzBrInTMXLT2yfNMiIQZzMKTcTerGIbjnOw_ArEB2GTI6GE3TWA12dTrkGDBUFS8tFYZcKQ_TDgoeZRbLF82wa3r82H5a-xBcpHfJUU42RUJxy1Kgk_OspC397jUxVOtro97xaJuv1ADdmCcLWlB5LmHc1KmvT50z_jy7wVdSYzznLdxlZ-Uk1g4Bo7Xv23487qTqTnumjicxX5EL0sA==> .

 

Agency Inefficiencies

 

According to an unnamed brand planning director who spoke to Digiday's Josh Sternberg, agencies are falling behind in the digital advertising landscape and, by his account, are completely inefficient. The unnamed source tells Digiday, "I could name a very large company who are currently paying top dollar for expert community management across multiple social presences. It's being done by a single intern with precisely zero experience." Counting Audience

 

Second-screen viewing, mobile TV viewing --they're all gonna get counted by TV audience counter Nielsen according to an article in The Wall Street Journal. The WSJ's Suzanne Vranica and Amol Sharma write, "Next week Nielsen will announce plans to augment its TV ratings data with information on viewing on tablets and smartphones, meeting a major demand of media companies that say they aren't getting credit in the current system for viewing on mobile devices. The change won't take effect until next fall's TV season, however." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwtcdSrUyNpXa4BNTzH8Y64H1BmmuMk3asAuZ7hd2MyXMrf_Enm_7T-1RtgrDZYVcEJCbEdNJt8w1qKe9UbnhoVvFuH9ApIwhCm442Q3klOOY_Dz_p0Fpyyc7y0BwW0jLoe1B6TwCppPMULBGbzBKdrDcT8WB2pFu_Mrwwy37jjNcytkXFZc0Jur> . "Twitter ratings" through Nielsen gets rolled out on September 30, says the WSJ.

 

This Is Programmatic

 

In an effort to educate the advertising industry about programmatic, the IAB has produced a programmatic and automation guide (pdf) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwudy02Jx09WLDighTElIcKPkCu3YK5xrTGgbdnearvvZpLFU2Hz-4N85D8deV2LNQNpNy-DYo6m_srKx1JJ7wO-dRP7a5lFF_eOZN52GVISrOx5LtyNq8nQ969Ml4asdzSGupQiDwrOtb6wSYEwbhKG2PRXksSmFcUUac3c2grkna8zC-gCLewbkXoIUYtdkfM=> . The paper is an attempt to narrow down a few key terms to describe all of the jargon floating around about the new type of ad buying and selling. This is the first in a new education series produced by the IAB. Read the article <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwvifrTeHd9bfRKeqCSBmYrTZZkbZp8Ne7EJBrSc570w6Que4xoJ9fIcVlgVjnHYeykwXX3Aa8k4sd08P7j8_KUR5b8raN1qcknOE0J0gQRFSRZjrB26K7DtSQ1pyS5pSlFd4uQTOraWSO92xzxYvs3Ce4dkUGqzCJRDtwQcCENZLr8IxM_bmvjEclq177gy55wcrcTxkFq6IvAEwLsEfb_H> .

 

Proving Ads Work

 

Facebook wants to prove its ads work, and this time they are working with telecom companies to show them how many people switched mobile carriers or phones after seeing an ad. Facebook has also partnered with Datalogix to show consumer packaged goods companies the effectiveness of their ads on the social media site. According to Alexei Oreskovic at Reuters, and Facebook, three of the top four carriers are taking part in the measurement service. "We have the ability to understand how the ads actually influenced the device that somebody had, and all that data sits within Facebook," said Brad Smallwood, who oversees Facebook's measurements and insights group. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwtiYCu8C-Sa5rBQ467zndBsBC44OtYKZJtzqL7ZOyMTuXaBPzgosseUPXavXzvHr7p3VDYXhSDgDmRpPHQMmky6XEdgM0mGT0VCesyfjfUpzqt_CZfmg3YCB5fUBZgieZgzaBvT52M4cxNT88j8Cd8pQn-_A3iMvfSCo223UMHktefgz8a4s6wTTKwFO_j2las=> .

 

Real-Time Faces

 

Reminiscent of Affectiva (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwurkD7NW4ajF-pXpJYn4GXOy2r3v94NhfIMZFjBXJZRcHu9Ro_4_R7w4MUG-RzTrte4oIgN0y1XETF9MzhcvrBq7O6iXi800I2Kcn3D35QepPT9CPK7kmxnF1Of-zLHvK80PQmfrYsedt-duUr7GGAUBH95T7wCLq4=> &A 2012), Marketing Land chronicles a new company's efforts to address audience through facial recognition. Called Facedeals, the company's CEO Dave McMullen tells Marketing Land that his company's tech allows users to take control of tracking. Marketing Land explains that "the app is 100 percent opt-in, 'If you're not in our system, we don't record or track anything about you. Consumers have the power to build their own profile and share it with brands when and where they want,' says McMullen." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015hTZllrCGwuYt1Dp281PwGGLqmloztByVUsXOfkfG739GONK52ew4YLM5ZpEBjLW1uWMbyjw45pUci0WGvahmXq4fWVjp4biSgGvfs2_vJcK9f2w7s2-XiAgZJMXPQ46Z-5Kk2UrdLyiw6P51KKRUMG98316sBI7K5Ji_N7cTumXhmOoNsY747C1jhBj_yeI> .

The Confidential Benefit

 

The ability to file an IPO confidentially is a great asset to advertising companies, according to Tim Peterson at Ad Age. Some examples include Marin Software, Tremor Video and YuMe, all of which filed confidentially, giving them time to develop their investor message wisely. It also gives companies in the fairly new online advertising a chance to avoid any negative backlash during the quiet period. "I can't think of a reason why someone wouldn't take advantage of it," said Tremor Video CEO Bill Day. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YEPOhslYNq_AySjmgG7GGjZ-qn2aCqmKFRneF6NcL_xK8Ba-me643Ac2G6YmdlNTP0M29AKYnSBNlCjhLw69v77sNFFoj1yg5OaZDrCexM5A0uAZBNpXIvUTYW_UWGSl4CiPs3B0Q8Ee8i0ddF2UDvY7ChlEBaXBmF-Mb_0HvR9n7jIAZHuj1OXT3IpQkwhGlY=> .

 

RTB Bridge

 

IPONWEB, led by CEO and Chief Scientist Boris Mouzykantskii (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YG2-0Az6OUL3qdQsVcV-4Rg1hA1beJmizKYhGp88qS9d2ldsleOePRhdzW0poRzY19DjtlA7t6Sqzqo7-dQDnXaXGO2uZoeae1j1mQsaGK2RAqT3H8CLCu3S8k1jqRJeh4gQPq0uoIn6ZLTeWaufckukPjC_uqsFkA=> &A 2011) announced the launch of a beta RTB integration solution called BidSwitch. The product will be a bridge between supply- or demand-side partners. It has started with display and will eventually enable other media such as video. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YH6Upz3ZA1nqWWAM9MVxcsOGYfYWHFVbSCOlwrjRl4GmNj3cHF-CJPecKF1036Y638MmY_hMX11xmtqDjfgYK-8o-rPSKAU030shOwKefBLnhBnaP8299iLXZzlYQgrCdjPTVFIMC526S1fmXe7uh_i5mmWNF8Ri6mTRPcb2aHAU5aNvUgpDzS9RpQ2em-ftQ74FHdpmnkFzKCl2iFSQIvA> .

 

Transparency Tools

 

AdFin says it is upping the transparency game and releasing a cross-platform price discovery tool. The company will also provide data visualization and BI tools. AdFin CEO Jeanne Houweling says in the release, "We're here to strengthen the entire market, and make it safe for more advertisers to move even more budget into digital." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YGxE4szTimrUxqfIKaIbeVFn7cBKH2FxeOl2Hv986rCbVZVTBR8ySTNYjOJEIw1UnHvTNAhnFkTIw1xEpIElIqpY90R51rm1scN7neaswUiAcEbcXmROEWuRHLaUgz81mY_29-kZYBCOYFStnPMsVU4zAlJkscRHPQ=> . This is another take on the Bloomberg Terminal, according to AdFin. Brilig <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YEk9UJj6sVfeo8sk3aBXRrvxGrZYdoXd7DIqaAIBiyWdr8ZiuCJN-uP3OZepmTHqh0nEyFgU5y3oQPwWL7LDluRzqz--QJJzVx8ZsVihHoWUhfamopDLVbhIXbPl3Rd9lNEL064ycuKgCY2269VbbITKmITSMc7QD2xVjoER6aIq-qflbB_0etcQXx2aCJiRSomKuuLs58TIheeHr2vLrdNP6plAwOrJeyPvJZsSWwV4XVv1eazKOao>  (now owned by Merkle), Visual Revenue <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YEXbb_jQTL5AoRiZuOL782zu9pjCRrO84x9RYXkSvOxYXm7XMAWCZfnsRPMLa4z3O_SqPIl5C51M1EeDlwDjV1nmV5TE0Hwr-JA3BfrBFELKzNH3T8fWG3iZVW-bgW9S3MpPs_KNHVmJWp5j1DjpOjPXsu22Y_yk64GZk3AW5dIAQ==>  (now owned by Outbrain) and MediaMath <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YE0Whp-Mqib3m0UZjqDG_F1ghbX2ncBaJb6DXcUeq64yCrG6AMpcksebEUlGtwoBCLoWzCT2ibNRaL026PbE9LOlh7o7vN37r6yh3lgbtpcCxL2VHtELJel4GmB4Bx2cWV6aezA_6i5alv09czANwniOYvml_RJnkOBJfqyFG8UQTCAAb-fYa2UkjjAHBrvwN8_Hz0RNcMdn8VwwDVwFBYJ>  have all had the "Bloomberg Terminal" positioning, but with different product angles.

 

Wielding The Power Of Data

 

Everyone talks about big data, but do they know how to use it? A Gartner study found that 56% of respondents who are planning a big data project don't know how to get value from the data. Matt Asay covered the study for ReadWrite, and his advice is for companies to start small and train in-house staff rather than bringing in a third party. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YFmSUb8YNJE0bYmsdTKgxGnGF_LL6CzM8FoJH7FXqSd-UHxr1Xiw3z7-TlH8NMneVXwYHFC2tyKqB4wDhm9iN6vAf_I63QCiggCgY60WCgS3HgD34NMCEp11tZsVchLwW8lieHrFPPH7JVvg0vfHnxce5yrBiL9BsQOb62j8_gPkTmdRymMzgL3_lCcb81ztouJeKTKhBwkBesyx7dkIdOf-a_WV_vzjwwzmthzXNmHZw==> .

 

Video Ad Pricing

 

Google is making it easier to watch YouTube videos offline, Peter Kafka at AllThingsD is reporting. In a blog post the company announced that users can store a video for up to 48 hours to watch on a mobile device without an Internet connection. Uploaders will have a choice of opting out of offline viewing, however. As Kafka points out, this could drive up prices for YouTube ads given that this creates an even bigger audience. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YEU9IC1bPFuvAKj7L7-5qzmUuVUVvCfLO717qk3FGzX5QGGOLvBMjKdzEaoP-JMozrjPE0VO_lBwMa9H4L1xgU7qCY9dOmAXD1b29l3vbeXjDHEZpQqnP8XuQrWqd1lvANx0qiYVdLpX6O5Kz2PlLFYFlMcHfZRiSHS10iTJY4lbOX4QipjrJj70oFWu04hbHwdrgOiWozpn3Pg2XHHDZkxryANPy-cxnpXUPTMR3EYjbElLEbFQRXx> .

Fraud Tracker

 

The industry needs the digital ad equivalent of the Bugtraq email list that is universally read in the security field, Spider.io argues in a wonky blog post. "Everyone in the ecosystem would be able to review and debate how best to secure the legitimacy of the ad inventory being traded. Everyone would also be able to disclose specific vulnerability details ... in much the same way that today's information security researchers disclose specific vulnerabilities through Bugtraq." More <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001k12o-KgQ_YFt_8djnt2dmF6LxhR1EVZWAAp6Jfoxi45kgXvd1wgXVfrMi-Ps6OtSPqoQ1t6M_TQw-cTnmkkYrlELCHw99TVC-6YXyu6HHhNhZjaDITiFRp94BBxyJEL5047Wj0DqZvCQH6E3UTfvnuoVOkjOGSfLHGe2V_4QbrpgsWO_zbRRcKqRxQU007zdpYiDjW1zUrEZdZhacxSAAw==> , including calls to action on terminology and taxonomy.

When Facebook Bought Atlas

 

Buried in a Medium piece on ad-tech plumbing, self-proclaimed "FBX creator" Antonio Garcia (who has left Facebook) recounts the internal reaction when the Atlas deal went down. "All the product managers involved ran to the IT Help Desk to get a Windows laptop to check out this thing we were supposedly buying. Believe it or not, Microsoft's Atlas only ran on specific versions of Internet Explorer... It was creaky and ancient, and possessed a flow so convoluted even professional ads people got lost in the mess." But Garcia says people confused by the purchase are missing the point. "For a modest sum, Facebook jumpstarted a presence in the display ads world in which we were an afterthought." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WGeaJYhsYhCGCV8zombVAvCzX0QHk4Wa66Jm1tKvq5lfU668vGpDj7Ny_XVk9jnxTBKettZqYQKIk4_w5FTW-VDnUzaoEpH6Ua4jtArUeomyhFgECUDCJG3bT2k68sWCXN0-JJ2e2gaO5wa8Cdw6YoG> 

 

New Tracking Tech From Google

 

Google is working on a new tracking tech for advertising (AdID) that could be a cookie successor, a source tells USA Today. "The new tool will give users the ability to limit ad tracking through browser settings." Unclear: Will this be limited to Chrome and its approximately 36% browser market share. A Google rep confirms, sort of: "We believe that technological enhancements can improve users' security while ensuring the Web remains economically viable. We and others have a number of concepts in this area, but they're all at very early stages." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WFeM-FItF6OdSIDvAzuk9YFdew63l5nm7XDUZ14veV1jy04TpkBaI98H5mH4Jkq22J8MJFntLyHlJCGWuWQZzTTuUWz7IMM78yVo6CqQ7g09W6gr4wY2R5w9k8TPGnGkSheJMaoRFlhyaOxvRDrTizgKf_x96yGd7ZQDXrfW_Ax3BVSCY0E1WHk1la2bFzOc2_hEiwrobLLtA==>  Unrelated(?): The Digital Advertising Alliance quit the Do Not Track group today and announced plans to work with browsers on new choice mechanisms <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WG79ySsBPDRH5ZfvQaC-sLcaeL_I43DIlh5y3UqU4r684kOBqF7TLNv9r11yYgHJwvZ7aosBps_JWqjXSqLhYNI8x2RdCba_Mzf3SXXT0En_wfyTsFFCdSqes02KkU6AoMBiHZJYlr87DKnX1mEl21CmEXiMintK6H1bcER1ktmmjGseXTNAl7ZTU0e4Z8TkLkGcymYFL91ZTUvux4q6l0w> .

 

Do Not Track California

 

California is enacting a new law that requires websites to disclose how they respond to "do-not-track" signals sent by a computer. According to Jeremy Mittman at Proskauer, the legislation also requires the sites to disclose whether or not other parties collect personally identifiable information. Regardless of whether the Web company operates in California, it will have to update the privacy policy to reflect these changes. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WGz-_czH4nrcakPqcGNu6z0kwyTxKE_OMJ3_kssUpD0ALTWjtBR-9uZC4TaGa97jYqAuNKWN6rw3-6bHmH-MKDibXY0H-oNDiH2HAG8vonYF6RG1AUtPIX_YBByLQZ-tICqMGSlUi742WpiTa7SAqgcqru0q3VCQjXxqYHd06cEh7QFDwLKupfannh-cDVvTwGKg6T3YpOwkjDsOygo79BeugmpQno_PSPxdmUNOpZNr4ApACJSrJN0dbP6kxduCiqmMn6EpFW1xIyRdQ4iH7lV5csVtf7X9Es=> .

 

Tracking Acronyms

 

There's a new acronym in town and it's privacy-related: TaaS, or transparency as a service. Enliken announced its plan to launch a new set of tools that will inform consumers about the data being collected so that they can be more comfortable with tracking. The platform will work with CRM and cookie data. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WGYWjrI9r7SsY9lPuj4cbq-AuCdh0pceoUXBCef21r1lZ0oJTSYnHz_qg2M9i4v-ys6FMSi1mJ2pLHjAu7S8EJ69JJ3qE2BgRM_nPl9CX64oBgxGvGbkkuktJoPR4q5L15MXCRb3j-kFO4G1LwgbFWzCw46b-ohGxQ3e0usH8kjIb9gqTXa-UitBLlH4iQy2xrK22oQks4QjQz23EeMawOb> . The new product comes after Enliken released its thoughts on consumer sentiment as it pertains to privacy. After surveying 600 people about their profiles from five companies, they found that only nine data points were rated as sensitive. Read the post here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WGSs4nedj6k_gbyoFbXdOyT7x3cvAJ741HC1WfMjobSpx86bwF6T13Sbs8fWE0KWR-W6hWLzRJZJoag7lsm1nyz4ezPS8sgPLa9qNwAHLLyI-qqx81NLaJSSynP_zUvnBciHXiexjCDCiS8ZWWKKBTQRKQi_OKPWb7jDMKOSI0c3W8p3KgOAdDsKW4l_2YOoYs=> .

 

More Than Programmatic

 

Doug Weaver, founder and CEO of Upstream Group, offers his thoughts on programmatic in a post on The Drift blog, echoing what he said at AdExchanger's Programmatic I/O conference. Although he feels programmatic may be a significant part of the advertising future, companies need to put a lot more thought into advertising than just a "dump it and leave it" mindset for impressions. He writes, "It comes down to will, commitment and leadership." Twitter's Simplicity Problem

 

Twitter's advertising approach has worked for the company so far, but if it wants to continue making big gains it will have to diversify. As Vindu Goel at The New York Times points out, Twitter has mainly focused on big businesses and limited data sets. This puts the company at a disadvantage against its social rival, Facebook, which relies on highly targeted and diverse ads. The MoPub acquisition is a huge step up for Twitter and a sign of things to come. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WFyCek9x5UxMIxCQagriiekVZHX1mEzw6cFqZJw4fWWuAaPeDAZqJDvaKGJ5bwG82jOIH8LXQ28PVRZknLtiiCXPvMTO_M2oD1hxg2rtVhI0e3kRmklCCx_74Pjju_1Q2O4oyfm9lifChTw9c0ZXtOAmY-wtJnQqbCr5nTkk0VFIYwuUj6oaVw04LQ7FPStpdqeotNg4XDkUNxL-dJpTqXYdTtLBrgHZq1wUXMk1vFoFw==> .

 

More Trust

 

Nielsen has found that consumer trust in advertising is on the rise after comparing data from 2007 and 2013. Even trust in banners ads has increased. "Brand marketers should be especially encouraged to find owned advertising among the most trusted marketing formats," said Randall Beard, global head, advertiser solutions at Nielsen. "This form of advertising is trusted by nearly 70 percent of consumers globally." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WH5ZZaoBj8R7pOXKIqsDCkW2v_P4NNQ89MnK0iAj0mWrGfMe__4nC5PGQif4rCfJhpyAe6AcGs4mvp1L9nZdVfd8190prSdUp0hGvLW8QyX3BYJ54NszdFCrWkCB6nQy4AA-gAByPZiI45uvh4SIXhfMwPlLrsVvrh_OIjN9dqk25o0Trz-jxkhXslTiqTVC-kJNUs-hcWEMxq151sbY3OX> .

 

Microsoft Playing Catch-Up

 

Microsoft always seems to be late to the mobile party, at least according to Matt Asay, VP of BD and corporate strategy at MongoDB, writing for ReadWrite. First, the company tried a horizontal strategy of licensing out its software, and then Apple got big doing the exact opposite, enacting a vertical strategy. Now, Microsoft is switching to a vertical strategy by buying up Nokia and developing its own hardware, only to see Google make huge strides using a horizontal strategy. Microsoft still has a huge market share in enterprise software -- Perhaps it should focus its attention on bringing that to the mobile table. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NVG7ICk95WHzJpGvbSftZt7oXtvzz98M4_5UfSvv51YloQNj-oSaoiNj__vB5Cx5gsZ39bUl9_16n2k_g12BSn0c64vw9RGguxoWzcTFUK9Da6I9VPy0jvkYkX_tvBnedmUqJoIWRYd7muUOhaqxv4jpg4e5XKzhiU_OHZ_CCU995cSETMbY_26-eVYVl7MpFtmPnEerv4uNlJy0JdHJ8dANU8-PEoT5JnSbDEpqZZuZIVeoGKfNLkHaHoIUegxQ> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTFdVViLX3yuXpxt2wdaDq6SsnKhFrv5y87NudwN-R2DAAkoYSJ661ilv-TJlsEQ_Ls77vKoqqJpi7VJvJ-mg5oxIKvsdlQw7r-Bj_p0fFWgt-ucBZ0PU9ZKbgOUjyUmz5M=> .

 

'M6D' Now Dstillery

 

Media6Degrees has changed its name after buying EveryScreen Media. "Dstillery is a brand idea that dramatically captures the essence of our core technology -- distilling mountains of data to produce pure brand-leaning audiences," said CMO Elizabeth Hellman. The company will focus on bringing offline and online data across all platforms. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTExQz3A_OFQtSrWgY_NU38alsz82ZGbW3GGjyk0nLQiNXpl7Ui1nCHWfVIO_FEcKllqkx-RncpKX1UtgHXkQSG9Qu_7MimpuC3hauN-jombrebnlVOHwnsXtgupVKfFkG5PtkKsKf2yEXG8V_Nw9lA3jRJF_dbLRvFLh9wheifZvK5tzU7tPD5issDjJvUNr73Pj6bmOeFALQ==> .

 

Beefier PubMatic

 

PubMatic is hiring up to meet demand for private exchanges. Alex Kantowitz writes in AdAge, "PubMatic is expanding its current staff of 350 by nearly a third. The company will also open four new offices, and set up three new data centers. In all, the total investment will reach $10 million dollars." Are agencies outsourcing some RFP grunt work to SSPs? More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTGCQNbdwmeBYT4q8vEpgA7g6PQHve1pib-BrdLEJqfushyp0kE6H3WgHuEC9tcSej5fVY99gqQzl4pCiGhyHn57Fb6ECdoqx0Do8VrSskwHz_VczH-Qa4cpw7LP8o84dW18FK-kbY_3t5qq0oCzOtJGFa7ZYZU_78fBaBnrl-deZrzaUz92MHA_duAEjiswnDKItWlUCPZ5vtSXTr8uBJrScrVlBb5VaiT_BLjo3PL18g==> 

 

Native On Notice  

Native advertising is capturing everyone's attention, including the government's. According to Jeff Roberts at paidContent, the FTC has vowed to hold a workshop about the new ad format in December. The regulator hints it may have concerns around disclosure as it prepares to "explore changes in how paid messages are presented to consumers and consumers' recognition and understanding of these messages." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTGlWOwIpYoTtHIaKH0O7w6eBs-4cdzz2EQ3Cz8oz2hiSil9TfILyrMN-sxyqy-bvW2B13JG6JLfeylybEVS5lgTltFkW9vObb-yJ9SH7oSgeRedtWQg33FjRuaHqGB-x10fYIdHi14DqhY79tucHcOaifhqgatrLFV1QlL_F1ET5C5fBuxM5miIlv6VllWlAxeHDmumDqMjyA==> .

 

Funds For Mobile Retargeting

 

ActionX raised $3 million in an effort to build out its mobile retargeting platform. The idea is to collect data with an IDFA (ID For Advertisers) and retarget ads for products people viewed but didn't purchase. An advertiser can then retarget in another app, or on the Web. "Last year was about driving downloads and moving up the app store," said CEO Evan Schwartz. "This year is about driving transactions in commerce and subscriptions." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTEW7QsqICG8d2opsUJOf25a00RqT4_slGWHgGZIC_9x-gowdiwXMM3HBvQZQG7LJas6tyw0XM2AbUNXJ5TL8AbKz5SgHyuwUc0OL1hDCwTVTa2KpqqezOzpvtI8aJA_lZwWrS692NeIjVgz83emihDXaXSq6dyvFGT3pgepB2699dJDwKNCdRjDHRmrxJyVqin6moAMfWxNoCQDIhFb5hBxXcjiAStyug90NtZh-fMuAkbPfPZ6fZmuM7qQsmRGbysi6PT5UyfkNE7gAtjyCK2I> .

 

Social Is For Everyone

 

Facebook may have growing relevance to the B2B marketer, argues Andy Lombard in a Marketing Land column. Lombard lays out eight benefits for using social media to reach other businesses. "Just as someone else might check out the Facebook page of a favorite band or clothing line, executives are likely to check out companies they might do business with." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTGrBcyCRDO2sI_41PQXN_8MXiTsn9PKAgYDwD4JDw9Q6dFVcXfwoH6BZVkWZdM0o6v92opZPuq_508KjuB_3zWoHnuyTs_9X_sy0cn9vKD3cgPsQGhWKHRFCXtm904WsHZppA1UvA-Sr_yOm1SjafWrhu741Fh9Jwf-w1JRAWeiY1KrTGcTzF4eeu9iiAcC10iIP5-JYPbc6_cZPnsECCm0IqbhtRbZF_U=> .

Facebook Mix

 

Analytics geeks often scoff at media mix modeling, but Facebook still sees merit in the approach to help clients evaluate social spend alongside TV. Inside Facebook reports, "A major retailer [unnamed] has already been using this data in their mix models to determine Facebook impact such as return on ad spend and volume per dollar spent, and Opoku said that the retailer has been pleased." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0018aml_ldWzTHnurfd1q1IHae-ihAbGBk_Id2glzAeOjaWIlPO9p9T5TkK-SFyY9d6azIUtEVRKdq08qja6vBClqtZVwn-dlN3Hu4_Q8AxP84GJerUtrh5ZHDrwUULS9cxSUEwQxGkW3IgjU8nKbA3mdAacYyMKX1oFdawGwW6OR4SvmUs9_lremXja5H4zJVSvEDXKRUlv8Ezv4EMAe__0u8XV6jXDDhaCvu7bHl6IKhud402nzcG-A==>

Competing Data

 

The search queries "marketing" and "technology" are slowly decreasing in frequency, according to Gartner, while searches for "Jay-Z" are increasing. The reason, Martin Kihn speculates, could be that Jay-Z does digital very well by using the channels in unique ways and forming the right partnerships. The rapper does have some competition, though, from Hadoop, which is capturing an increasing share of search queries. Read more from Gartner <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ09AzHG00MOpfbcUwprF6T6RxIa5356j2zKpffgsZCeRhybJzU4CY_fQxai-lJ2VQDW12bOku4cw3hdcM74zP7hfp5qPcQ2ipqZs3eyi88Swte8MLlqX5e25cczytF6heWlzwAJH2868zLWySSMEkYynM-ZzN5wBUp4xwvbuRyBVqBEyOggMBaGu> .

 

Inaccurate Data

 

Industry execs tell Digiday's Jack Marshall that much of online targeting data's inaccuracy -- such as third-party demo data -- is real. Marshall's sources say "the problem persists largely because buyers of the data, mostly agencies, tend to turn a blind eye when it comes to accuracy. But it's not just agencies. Like many aspects of ad technology, plenty of middle-men are incentivized to make an ad transaction happen whether the data being used to inform it is accurate or not." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ0_ho7a3lxwMVCy3do5SZg4acyED54bGtfrOqU6tr_4UYbXd0-03uZ2QhRNItOunQfATCPX-2oJri4TxfVu2MsONiYky7oLW9l4f80oEGTm0ewIl4r-1OT9WHN7ioFWEr6nQaZ3_sp7HX8IMEnp0eLbYqqr_3Z-H2QC3QYV5MSaBUg==> .

 

Medium Momentum

 

On iMedia Connection, Eric Picard ponders momentum of digital and traditional mediums. He concludes, "If our industry can get to the point where executing media buys across traditional and digital share a common process until the moment where they diverge from a delivery perspective, I think the market overall will make great headway. And I'm bullish on this -- I think we're not far away but it won't happen this year." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ0-B9WI1ykHCU8PV6opZTYmJLT9MIsZltQqu9bo6d3bpzweSVllPnk-q4EYugtFjApilH4ej41wxQNOJxk6ldNtpeuTR5EkQHBD0zBzAepI8OBneud8MGsvbcVt4PMRngOTr2-lPM4j9w3RwZUpuryZb> .

 

Programmatic Milestone

 

Mobile ad exchange Nexage CEO Ernie Cormier takes to his company's blog to review the Twitter-MoPub transaction <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ08hiGrOgcI6gtKSyPTPwgerAb4XWUhZXQJwts0ws3gZU2jO8pbBDf6tSLkohpZTxk-moqqWGyvMT3mQzvkiN_mZ4rDoX59HiXQ__RrYkYDUMZ2uEqaU9ybq3B7sJoNZ3osEkzEobzMYj9QzaSrlL25Eu8uPPvfV1qMg4g46KkoEX54mP5YNFvO24OYPvnQZ3Mg=> , "... Let's not underestimate the meaning of the transaction. It marks an important event in digital advertising - it moves the industry from contemplating the importance of mobile, programmatic and the power of data to taking real action." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ0_yp3zeRh-uY5qLengsMyw0b1tkQ95u1uA_mHt3ml6Sl712-5gBIiWJT-Eg33SK9B0pbbKOrctt5TPqymRgyZJma4uZ0DEoUb2yRplrG7lXZsFZiDVRwHRKP8nu3FW4ZrJcsn3m-CxHHo32dbCktbpXdZBIMWCIyqtjux3Yp6VEE0y_bsZ9Ob2H9CCftQEX4pHJEcQdccqKl6jbeuueRoW6> 

 

Facebook's Ascent

 

Ad Age surveyed its subscribers and found that over the last 15 months advertising on Facebook has gone from experimental to a necessity. About 74% of respondents said their Facebook budgets include Facebook ads and 43% reported that their ROI has dramatically increased over the last six months. Mobile likely has a huge part to play in that, which reflected well in the climbing Facebook stock price. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001uxOJJQFPJ0-PQEYHfiJL06DE0JBoBehtgupShT6eI9xY9865mxOXHOLmMRMStEus31UWzbJsD7bhW4HVDsO_t79gkeJ4D76AXz_cPY7skpxE8fep9fKFPgqcsF665hmm9BaCDg4r2Y-lhXFtMjk0ovWPcSABDFQePyUMlReFokAVxdR_Sc7r41L66bAhxaJI5ZpClTgx6vCwzg_pUVKKpA==> .

Real-Time Branding

 

Twitter's got one thing that a lot of brands need: real-time data. Mondelez is creating a partnership with Twitter, according to Emily Steel of the Financial Times, that will embed Twitter staff in Mondelez offices in Brazil, India, the United Kingdom and the United States. "The whole point here is being able to react to what is being talked about in culture in the moment when it is being talked about," Bonin Bough, vice president of global media and consumer engagement at Mondelez, told the Financial Times. "Twitter is constantly evolving their platform and technology. Being able to be close to that is a huge opportunity for us." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5OhDeFd2ZuOLL6uAgMmKLb6sbmpq1BqbK9uxi-4oFIyFi9N6nxSvOum8bbmxyshYTDsnDwIsLvsV_K7KqGxxNAFwPeQqwq9w97i1-qXdZ3hM17inSxu90kc1cU_aTNbpnoAXO0BQQC_4Fl9CvoLcKTBNVYsEtjiy_Vlnsxk5Djcfw==> .

 

Checking Out

 

There is a difference between check-ins and location sharing -- one is declining and the other is rising. Screenwerk looked at the difference and found that while people are no longer checking in with services like Foursquare, they are still sharing their location on social media. Facebook is at the top for location sharing, and a Pew study found that 30% of people have set up automatic location tagging. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5NiDhbEDEGRV_97egPM1ZBTY_ozROUmngqhwknTz12fBnNZeSctkIS81WFcJi9D2BZVuU9T0vLnxAsT_1AUop6Ue8Nct_5xxQ92Rt8Driaxdf4inLQIZ7xHxFwaPJG0io_n1AVdSrulFOtWTfkT9Q4bSw93F88xk3PLQVHa7Q1ji8FPyHPQSYHZJzEZm7j8k8XOAJPk5hGISh9nxhP9wahY> .

 

Internal Tech

 

As part of yesterday's announcement <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5MILdXCam29KzBFSiev1L3rjfuJ4PHu3wPnSYyMRFg63DL1UaDM_X596TJIWItjsx_nU7NGxs4KgpnLu5LhsZCnLm-PI2Ioehf7-aLQoFdbo1m0YELgcZ2Xmd--va1zALt9DoGgga8gPmGe2rzwXiFtOXSwmGCN0hFgvQRpIHSZHiTazy1k7mAVU2eaJa0PAT3UR75PqtsrNqBg53Fz2l2Sh7QLBncjUTJLfhI4ENLXbcP42E8NKBMw>  about an update to Adobe's Target product, AOL's director of retention marketing, Jen Towns, offered her client-side view to Internet Retailer: "The amount of optimization testing Towns' team has been able to accomplish in the last year with Adobe Target would have taken at least three years going through AOL's internal technology team, she says." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5Nn8R2x6nDvj1-L8BHjZzNjy2VavMODey4GtSeaRcWSg3NsAhLZXenZPdXnzHhtpITMXKoLiSiSk_JqWk4h1s8ItO0bvOgZ1FFoZ1TDyyNTi7kXmYv7_6A8VejoS6u5dGo3wztOHTkQbNgESUpS6im5XJa9SapfBC_j8jSYb16LF5lg-B99NtZBCNKC0567lyI=> 

 

Twitter Revs, Still Sub-$1B

 

Twitter's IPO is real. "We've confidentially submitted an S-1 to the SEC for a planned IPO. This Tweet does not constitute an offer of any securities for sale," is what the tweet <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5PaSuUAtk9O-5hLcPfqyt0YrPPFu0vpBKTQZS2LM_irKTn0wjI2VJiOdUW6iw_jtPGJH8mGe5HM4Rhr6XrDFgzoJsjuGwePm1jZ3lTs1XbN4uHXyX5UHryBPo4tSCtt_JEFtkUQPA8SxJiX3vrtQcOk>  said. For the moment the S-1, and the company's financials, will remain secret thanks to a law allowing companies with less than $1 billion in annual revenue to keep things on the DL. More on  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5MCPKOOQ4s7gLMYcJOrJJHeEX4Y2BMQB5na5JaBv7LJ0QdMmtbB-6FL89fjP-pYiurHsjudAafZgRhv6wnDlWb_kX42sSo_MJk967cXkyRW-PyQo6lDMZ_DXW0Hjfy4HY6XfGfZG0bgK12iv1XH00uH9_U3R6NYNzNg200CB5nfmpBysSXG0eLqnySrU0H9WwXweW-8Q0o83xpct8R846C3qUS5WF5y9uw=> "confidential" S-1's from Inc.

 

CEO Boosting Ads

 

AllThingsD's Peter Kafka talks to new Pandora CEO Brian McAndrews about his experience with Microsoft and his new role with the streaming music company. AdExchanger covered the hire, announced yesterday, which you can read here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5PZCI9k9Aq4IDnVYgm0M58eCAldKf6n9loKTayPWWM0ZJklwMAWaVAE8m8LB1uqwgo8lewVAKDjhkOWtFCOozb3z9VCs0gi6Bna5lk4dLBNc-Wk-ntGXDBUlU8s_5MpT2hIwRSJqPPU_VKNvPrMOf5coz3X9OkwlGkITK4UBqn_GsVu0VaZgWCCWdYJdPzOq9fX1Tfv_gEidal2pty-mwGW> . Although McAndrews admittedly has a lot to learn on the music side, including about Pandora's ongoing battle with licensing fees, he's got advertising chops that Pandora needs now. "Mobile is still early, but I think Pandora has done better than a lot of companies -- better than most companies -- in terms of monetizing," McAndrews said. Fundings Ads

 

Addroid founder Matt Cooper hopes to reinvigorate banner advertising with banner video ads, and so far it's working. The problem, as PandoDaily is reporting, is that VCs aren't willing to invest money in the company despite its success. It would seem like he should just forgo investor dollars, but he says, "I haven't been sitting around waiting for permission. I built my business and it's making money." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0012Qr0vdR3G5O70PAbWeLHnCLO7VIev-ygbGBhldKGjLy4cV-0B4F6NctJygSDAd20Inawr9KcmXNKOnp0e2_u5vEC9aFKIcHb5_6t2V8AEUHTWsbSAJMexjwHQmZk7AzRJD-d5R4LcGnmtA-yBV87iQoMEtikAjypfyftUu9lYt2SnRLBrcsXBBvMBSaWSMYklkEp-Nbyneo1-fLY0WpaR9xGDeLkF-ms> .

 

Digital Ad Wallet

 

On MediaPost, Joe Mandese reviews agency Carat's predictions about global ad spend. The agency sees 3% growth, rather than the 3.7% growth it predicted earlier in the year. Furthermore, Mandese quotes the agency's report as stating, "Digital spend predictions continues to meet expectations of taking one out of every five dollars from the advertising wallet in 2014." Adobe's Cloud

 

In an attempt to make testing across all platforms simpler, Adobe is rolling out changes to Adobe Target (was Omniture Test and Target), ZDNet reports. Some major updates include mobile app optimization that will allow marketers to "deliver different, targeted experiences to app users based on engagement metrics" and a "Visual Experience Composer" that gives marketers more tools for quickly swapping out content on a site. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLEWES4qeW8BJ5GD2g6uHHhMRg68zxggc1lAokbP8hzbjEzOCKt3ZmOFkNfMMpifU_U0G1kXJN93LtcvEr_jTxCVHW6XgKxSxfqYtlMEOo9dQPElqQolvcDSpWaOtr4G2fZso2rKuqY5OuIPMDVK4ZAbA-YGWH0UmQ8uLv5K-12Xvd3D9yQJiayKHaIwRIrGWtCNa5vA0HbOKA==> . And read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLEvosck_ZytWIzjk-0arEosGv0PlG5MFRUllFCqCiYlTmDct-So1yvwx0nkxJap-h-J5vAjgoI2Ab9OZ3X4NZISNh4jZ-jIUwwFLElnu_-pk67jklEcGX0ZEtmRJ4uhI4UVta-S8YvWZ-V5qOOZi_fHNb-AQThKYJc3qvLNMOMOTnKNjq1A-4BnYmAbpYnHdfZdO35NebLM6UPguO4MkJLNlGwJo7xzR2WuRIQlqJioxYLs1aaakiVY> . Adobe CMO Ann Lewnes discussed her company's use of the product and the Adobe Marketing Cloud with AdExchanger last year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLE2FXftgjdB96oe0qeoLq1lX1D1unlx3Z1US1QduvfVr2zyN2HqQz3cIhwJ6x-rQgM5epaCN5P3wp6mdqB8Q-bUhbyzP508L5F8umtiI5lXdlra_wGOrgYz5k_CtlfuvtJUc_JYErIj20Xm1EvIJ8m_QTbmxlJUtW5jebclbJcxOEZtHSr4YBgIcQ8fJN9oXCVhPg_cstI7pz7WE4z4kSgzLlORUtVXsdM=> . Clouds, stacks...will they come together as a Clack or a Stoud?

 

Short Opportunity

 

There's no doubt that people are watching video on mobile, but is the advertising opportunity as big as advertisers hope? Adweek covers a Freewheel report that suggests mobile video is not ideal for advertisers because of the short-form nature of the format, and the small screen size. Ad video lengths, however, are getting longer, says Freewheel, as 50% of ad views are 30 seconds long - the same length as TV ads. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLGZFz0Fc6APgRjqdxTPIlOJO__YJ07OWFWxhlUiYPwfYjS8FimxACmfYCg-pSs0hLujiXvEt2w8CRqTterYoCZIyuJNf3scxbFRQLiWEPlefTejBBBYY542YmXPFUtVLzmGkDU5xV8XUn-0yLh4Sr7whXxU6mrvEp0vctk7JRyiaDMjFpfuwytM-qia51nTsY52uETufm7GVg==> . And download the report (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLG-HOYsFxfz1n9KdsrPPm7SzMc5POc9V_90tqXisGMTew1XKYA6t0u0UMmByGCB9en9SZWWXlVdqA-GSHuSGXvqfqiVMJ_Mo1Bpf-a24XSpcZAodyOogBRCfmHSW4buplKzlYmhpcZxSHhcoW_tuUaiHS42lI4CQGnaON4Iaa0ryqe6CgsJ7CSh> .

 

Patent "Brawl" Update

 

The comScore-Moat patent dispute (first reported <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0013RC5b3aOWLGw611_lS6-PURzHhtX9o8j8F7JfTrcAw-ErkhpnG0SXWL3J-CvUUvjQ8yLsQEhBCF9LO5xJH5b92a8I4eaXAY_jsHl1OuNmBidh8ZLAFGbX742jQ-o6uHVEvjWeOm3j02c8h4-RGN3E7E-9YuhSbFypPKboyI7uxOot1Nh42ik1A==>  by AdExchanger in July of 2012) continues in U.S. courts, as PandoDaily's Erin Griffith reports. A 23-page emergency motion to adjourn the trial was filed by Moat earlier this week according to Griffith, who reports, "The motion included argues that the trial be adjourned based on comScore's disregard for the court's orders. It outlines the way comScore missed nine deadlines for producing discovery documents like email records, cancelled depositions at the last minute, did not make its chairman available for deposition, and refused to answer questions." Strengthening Twitter's Location

 

The Drum covers more reaction in Europe to Twitter's acquisition of mobile ad server and exchange MoPub. Performics' Andrew Pringle says, "[T]he MoPub network provides a wide range of demographic and location data, allowing advertisers to be very specific with their campaigns. At present, whilst Twitter's targeting options are improving, plugging into the wider MoPub base will instantly strengthen this, specifically with regards to location." Your Ads Are Going Public

 

Content-recommendation firm Outbrain is taking steps toward an IPO, including hiring its first CFO, Jeff Davison. According to paidContent, the company will make an estimated $130 million in revenues this year. Israeli news outlets, including Haaretz, are reporting that the company values itself at $1 billion. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxdIJK0h1R32ttJS47QJSr0aiDzCIvyhsWTJiQLogo1Tc9YupsxLfKm5Ocxx8JTJ_fFvybseb5VffQ3YKQyyVD-r_dzVfUuJSwTl9Tpc3rreh7vVcR8yns5d9IVvrA55UoS_Cs-RhbXdkNx_0NOC5Rs9ib3jGm1ib8Vacu66NeOlPGWyPA7x_vUEiMr4vdUPcevN70X7E9ZV5mJt8lhOSstR> .

 

Mobile Native

 

Former <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxf0gC5Fb251mDo77mu8A_eLP6WV7OaSckiItCv3JkLEHzoJyad5DIvR5BohBaroMp7WZNWUlMQonUV4Zidqdaa78oM_rjgS_nqcDt1dOU_R65q0SYRZl7A4yQ9aNphBNIUe9cwztYXMi7EnblsO8N8K99soC7GLyg1ZMI-k49NWMw==>  One Riot CEO Tobias Peggs, who is now CEO at Aviary, hails the arrival of native on mobile, proclaiming that it will effectively kill banners and make companies lots of money. In a Tumblr post, he cites Twitter's acquisition of MoPub, Instagram's impending ads product and Snapchat's brand relationships as evidence that native is coming full-force to mobile. He writes, "Mobile advertising is dead. Long live mobile advertising. The native kind." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxdMvR9jT6Wxtq0jbMb1LE9vJFAsxszWWr-H8MOE9I7SPiUcMKzPENcGO5mQIKOYaCQVNUm5EFUAEOD5sdAIfee9JVxE_IGm02F5RwnIXeBbC8Bgw3Rg1af669B2MeA_BnoM8IREGhdNB-6MJJTYbkBsZDV5fPhrBoMgSWGpSC8ryO3W4467iettv21OzGzMCGuVjRphOvZITQ==> .

 

Video Growth UK

 

The rise of video is a global trend, and BrightRoll has released a report detailing video consumption in the UK. Overall, 85% of UK Internet users watch online videos, with an average of 300 videos per viewer. Programmatic buying also is increasing, with 41% of agency respondents expecting to dedicate half or more of their budget to programmatic. Read the report here (Pay with some PII) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxd_gtVyYKApaD7YNBvxuBSHalODkl1h5uTDCXzPT8PTs5cYvcEaktMCLWvX2NByaJGa1jr0nAGTjPCulShqR2rTFxEwtv8lZyc2wG_4HG864RP0H1bzxMDaU_QPu4p2HwRJ4eGramiaepsDt38J-3fE3_-_iprit67dNdJa3pWAOQvhcYrZB0xnmf99SAmj7GqV5hUnW3mrjCVZvpjoX_Qr> .

 

Publisher Rolling Dice

 

Rumor has it Time Inc. has been in talks with American Express about taking over the banking company's magazines, according to Ad Age, although neither company has officially commented. "[Time Inc. is] taking on essentially more risk," said Ken Doctor, an analyst with Outsell. "In the middle of their own transformation, they're doubling down on very consumer-oriented publications." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxdSTkZ1mgPNes3az6WmzYVNaptj8H5hdlVj3s8zQfxX-Xf_dF3TDGgKlcnuAc_GvV0GmMtnaTn_BryJmA7vr4DA56J8VggtASgOg4cIeNmAV6HOoaIxzlSd8w8TqhVYnXTRMDxuCznCFDwR1YcGp29cOJt5-eHfcff0kCypcerlzqR5b_Zc8hn0e6VjiSpxM16qRUbtBdQc_Q==> .

 

Searching Loopholes

 

Danny Sullivan, founding editor of Marketing Land, questions whether Google's protection of user privacy was really just a play to get more ad dollars. Some of his reasoning stems from the fact that Google left open a loophole that gives its advertisers access to search referrer data, and made it harder for third parties to compete with Google. Furthermore, in order to access search data older than 90 days, publishers must sign up for a Google AdWords account. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OD6Afa5uaxer_TFVIElBP0Diu7niNHck2n6b18IPG6yB96BWNr2f1I7MeVIaJiBloKv0eKv6lOlz1vs69ywXczp462C3LlFFtKFGaOcXEC4z_edCkP8QEQHuhxF_ppfvLkrcITbUCdB3cnl6TTJ8K72LUqb_KsE12jb3Ha-EEe4=> .

Trending On Facebook

 

Facebook is testing new ways to capture trending topics based on public discussions, much the way Twitter does. The initial partners, according to a Facebook blog post, will include Buzzfeed, CNN, NBC's Today Show, BSkyB, Slate and Mass Relevance, with plans to open it up more in the future. The two APIs will be a Public Feed API -- a real-time feed of public posts about a certain word -- and the Keyword Insights API, which aggregates posts about a certain word in a given time frame. Read the post here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8f1OO5PUQtPPSHH8WU1kUgfhaBwhm8_Y7IUoBAFUn5_6g__3PUFGG2aEdQ2N1njZ6sBRfufAVyHrNEkkyERJ_d3IEjLIXwSbBYCKrQIX318-2LHdM6kBlzD9ip1Kh_6lDEYg4UDg6ls3KEB9hsjXo0tOVgW00qZJ30-eed5ZSPeeyCe9AGwQ8mkf8BcpgI3hXo=> . And more in The New York Times <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8dAyQWHU18DuiifaL6f8SlWy-cwxMsJyOGvz7NClCbEg_APO8KKaNfXjBG13KmugfZwuOhgUVcA3JEWFu0I7r9NMSkZl8L2pTEJzfPcvUGtlbOpv_KcHv8oLmHa4hoz9wnq7oGQim8xsKEon9hOHTUDf1GVVsAqYs6Rvg33UcJNxqU_A-0GG0RTy12FeSovdSOlOW4wxb4maVK6s_ejuOoBAL9ChaKYbnM=> . Sponsored Facebook trends shouldn't be far behind.

 

TV Style Programmatic

 

In the wake of IPG's Mediabrands unit announcing <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8d_go154erPza3iKKUVc1K5L-UIylfJulx3daLiazqbhuEmmf53cEsiVa9brGdRbADTZGdZfOm1XguXzdgDOYetUuD5W67VT3hB53JzC0ZP7N8oVUjoOPpA7lIVlK6rZhqbBraN_KT_uGHsTcJ7mq9glpg9kaGwh9p5SCWsBAAa8cCe_eF7xozYdTR3Nx9E3UEPQLkqcJkaSAC94sZ3t-Me>  its TV-buying platform, WPP and GroupM's Xaxis says it's bringing TV style buying and programmatic buying together, according to Adweek's Mike Shields. The company claims to be working with Hulu and Viacom initially in an effort to keep the inventory premium. "It's long been my opinion that much of the ad tech developed is wasted on direct-response marketers," said CEO Brian Lesser. "It could be much more powerful for brands and upper funnel metrics. Right now, video is the fastest-growing part of our business." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8cq6cULoW1ld-dJsfc7m6ZrEjeN-7OsA5Ay2glJOIAHwe-1SFbPnOlIGldvxcmCFVHmoyUdCGEgiqhW0JF0FQplD09aXycdGBjIk9U7V2fc9lL8w9npXcNs-hoqBRoOeQmnLtd0TW1CNiE25EzCzfE7lFFgkEFAeTp0Z43mlL75aX4ZeHzzS2uSCM4kTK7_Ol4=> .

 

Instagram's Ad Future

 

Instagram was a huge acquisition for Facebook, but it's a company that doesn't make Facebook any money yet. According to The Wall Street Journal, Emily White is in charge of taking the small company and turning it into a profitable business without alienating its coveted user base. Advertising is the logical step, but brands will want to see hard numbers, which currently isn't possible, before they dedicate money to a free service. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8dzxhnGx1pSKsoC69ODdxbVovvNZg73ldNg2tjHiUCgHj_EoGKZi8p5JK6kVsjoWmo85p54Sm61Rnq4BLWy5kmrtArn2G9U5rR35lu5uXPgvbdOyhpjKCgroKMSoq6DP4qY2npeR9F-wQqQLVYgeiwI9IZxFwo8K1mHo5lkvjxmoxsUR-219TzQ> .

 

Mobile DSP

 

Mobile marketing company Placecast <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8d1Q8SuTdt_X04VVdmnShQ3UHl-YJ92jnBwATHF9rqw-6RB3705yZ2nCkwFeNVTKvLav-o8C1FSCP3v2srRUjX1epjBfRcumb9pGKM6KAFBGA==>  -- not to be confused with Placed or PlaceIQ -- announced its new mobile demand-side platform, called PlaceAd, which leverages location-based data among other targeting attributes. According to the release, initial supply partners include PubMatic, MoPub and Smaato." Read more (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8cGgJrd-O_T4vKV6uHYDCAwP27XgIrkY2gHzZmllY_57IRdGxHPhIbGfDon20H9S9sxQNHiyCwTH-6m8m7uUws8tyEmwhhpF9L5zpq-y4b-Jq5rmfYsiJkCGP2r5W2mC0SbzgX7H9pMTxCN8P7t05G1kyilT3Y26H7etTNOQzgwyQ==> . And read this Oct. 2012 AdExchanger interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8cslL67p_5zKXB3iuv1LTjM8q8eltS5OnH-eaLrZk4wRKtnm6dmEAubNH10IiHjE-3IJ5YrFwttedhW2vPHgCfd7MPA7XMUaA1sWzuBaTrcw8FIjlo4g8AB8mOaIsIlm1jZ3RFdn4j-9i-_yx8V2G4Qd4XZcosYwzXDJ_pwCTukcrlHFwBmes_256hMBX9HBOlOCs-Xb_emG9n_yBTEUl0s8JIZsjWdZvU=> .

 

Ad Countries

 

Speaking at Kenshoo's K8 summit in Sausalito, Calif., on Monday, Facebook VP of Ads and Ops David Fischer says his company's ad revenue base isn't just about the US. The UK, Brazil, Indonesia, Japan and, yes, even Dubai are among the key contributors. Read more on Inside Facebook <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8fEggMQJYmCs37fiED8XWU9nb6Gj_iC51d-KOJTcPJDdTAz4T3vDns6yf3G7Ikh8ehUQCkFY5M5iAV5dYn2EO2gnI0K69YZxn4VabVDd8qJBbqQEAwMkeUHuaZy5HdGzh-NScfPPyGdLv4pc-PzJSPNprX2UrioZEWQ-C0TZ2HcIx2LAyOw4e3AVOBN2clDhjdQeDCpdtM-Cs1BWryCNwNfTFVYLjcYO7s=> .

Data Bridges

 

Data continues to pile up, allowing extremely specific ad targeting. CRM companies will be at the forefront of this new age of data solutions, predicts Dana Hayes Jr., group VP of global partner development for Acxiom. In a column for ClickZ, Hayes Jr. points out that marketers can now target people instead of cookies. He writes, "The precision of the offline CRM is desperately needed in the online world to eliminate the waste associated with some techniques used in the advertising world today." Energizing Yahoo Video Screens

 

Energizer, the battery maker, is sponsoring Yahoo's expanded comedy video content across desktop and mobile. The portal is billing it as the kickoff for its fall comedy season, as it looks to build out a cablelike channel of short-form videos like Tiny Commando (it was introduced at Yahoo's NewFront presentation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001eD3Eu8NkI8cppziIxY8-Hcw9hCT0jv6ag7ULZHnf75OuMhMKxcuy4G5Qkkxaj1u7rGqC0PxfTbiUQ3Ux6L6odk_iU1rHnFo-xgRxkg39Wici9JLY6Y6tjZPFziGR3zSXl9jyM15FbYrFz0HyqeaM9-92gQDD1vWGKIF86aQo-_gSBTIDlRh_xsQ6X5Cq6EhTCE6b09Vcvj7Jd04HyI8yQ49-s773PTAmDx9a1Mj5TGqFlig9XHmBZQ==> ) and classic shows, like Saturday Night Live. "The way people consume media is changing, and the way brands participate in media consumption is evolving as well," said Brad Harrison, VP of marketing for Energizer North America. The humor and innovation behind the Yahoo Tiny Commando comedy series is a natural fit for Energizer, and the integration within the shows creates a natural brand experience for consumers also.  News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
